.1 girls letter from Ta.smanfa.
rnnou hast clean senses, as we have the
sense
Of things wherein no healthiness can
be;
The beauteous world is thine without offence
In sky, or sun, or least anemone :
r or thee a bank of cyclamen, green thickets
dense,
, -V soaring lark carolling liberty:
I'or us (lie bronze of every plume and shard,
.-nd all the beauty of the good world marred.
On the vast tragic stage of war we stand.
And wait our fathers’ crimes return with
steel—-
The ancient crimes to steal a rood of laniT.
To reive the stranger’s cattle and his meal :
Family. and tribe, and clan, and robber band.
r trampling beauty with his horny lieol;
Idle. herded millions, hungry for new meat.
Felling the fat and wealthy at their feet.
And then a crazed ambition reaching out.
Through slaughter, to that heaven—Ad-
vertisement ;
Ihe lust of gain, with beast-like cry and
shout,
Frighting the world, by terror almost
spent—-
Tartar and Cloth, in victory and in rout.
Burning through fief and hereditament;
And all earth’s beauty and her offerings
Dragged at the chariot-wheels with captive
kings.
two thousand years a town by Tiber made—
Home, builded by the genius of men !
Kinder than man is Time, and did not fade
It: holding it for genius yet again.
Yet. in a da.v. Alario’s (lothie raid
Left art but dust, and palaces a den ;
As Beauty in the grip of Death did stand.
W hen Tamerlane was lord at Samarcand.
Xet from old Rome beauty o'er-ruus tlie
world.
I 1 or once the world had but one nightin-
gale—-
AMiat though upon the capitol is swirled
But dust of dead men. and of powers that
fail.'
f lame of hereditary pride was hurled
Northwards, and clothed barbarians in
mail;
And. though the slaves were crucified and
rent.
The Roman slavers were magnificent.
Cmsar’s triumphal entry into Rome.
The naked dancing girls who strewed his
path.
-Made men forget the men who would not
come
Back from their graves amid the Gallic
wrath—
Romans who rotted far from Tiber’s home
To fertilise new fields: to grow a math
For bread to feed new armies—new to die
Fighting without a foe. not knowing why!
Rome did not falter, and Rome never shook.
While Roman guards had work for glaive
and mail :
They made their gods of qualities that brook
That man may do aught—anything but
fail;
Their deathless gods, who manlv manners
took
And scourged the coward as with thong
and flail;
Their gods that never die. if they be sooth
Beauty and Courage! Knowledge! Golden
Youth !
Aars caused by naught—king's mistress and
a prince.
Fimp of a back stairs, blind to that he did !
Dispute of Rope and parson, then or since.
Whether Christ’s blood is in the sacrament
hid.
AN hat though the spring in blossom of the
quince
( ried to them "Joy!" the fools would not
he bid ;
( hristian slew Christian, as. in centuries
gone.
Darius impaled his foes in Babylon.
The churchman in his cell praved loud and
oft.
With eloquence of all the Litanies.
And lying psalms from out the organ loft,
And blessings on all ills Jehovah sees;
The while they tithed the fold, and field, and
toft,
Their prayers found soldiers for Chancel-
leries ;
They prayed at home that God might win
the day,
And. praying still, sent men to burn and slay.
Always the priest to gird the soldier’s glaive;
Or woman—equal sentimentalist—•
To sing the song of glory or the grave:
To hide the facts of life as in a mist:
To call Almighty pity (that men crave)
By tone of voice or turning of the wrist!
The church that made for earth not any-
thing.
Halving the people’s labor with a king.
Glib marionettes of war whose instincts fled !
The cave man fought but cold and igno-
rance ;
In war with hunger, nakedness, he bled ;
’Gainst beasts and poverty he lunged the
lance;
Then through the ages, naked and half fed,
Man tamed himself, and then he found
Romance!
Art helped him to self-conquest, helped by
Time!
And tyrants sent him backward to the slime.
They make their wars wherever man has
made
A little plot to call his own on earth.
That love and labor diggetli with a spade.
To keep from some beloved the winter
dearth ;
With Love and Art and Music it is laid
Down with the soldier-dead —for a rebirth
When, with new spring, from out that gorv
hell.
Rise bloody grapes of Rhine and of Moselle.
Spoiled harvests, reaped by children and
grandsires—
olga and l)rina. Rhine and Meuse and
Seine;
Millions of men by winter's battle fires.
M here snow comes as the dead men's
chamberlain :
M lien artists, poets, wakers of the lyres,
Fall to the guns of clowns in old Cham-
pagne !
“God governs all !" Then men have steered
the storm:
For if God gave Man Life. Man gave God
Form!
Science' prolonging life, and slaying it:
1 he weakling nursed, and strong men cast
to die:
Tlie cause of Murder quoting Holy Writ —
Cretin ! who cannot know that he does lie!
And men of knowledge, or of lesser wit.
Go out to kill, as men with brain awry—
Lutcher and lamb ! Slayer and slain in one!
And knowing nothing when the slaying’s
done!
A war without a “God" can never be!
Without that name no thief can square his
sin :
His sin with self, and call self “Deity”—
The sneak, the murderers who with blood-
lusts win,
Pirates by Right Divine of Piracy;
And they, like craven David, that: begin
To steal a soldier’s wife, as Scripture saith.
And give the word that easts the man for
death.
Dead soldier who shall miss the joys of life.
The glistening bridal, and the " pomp of
gold ;
His ears a-dnlled by war-drum and the fife,
To all the things his dear affections hold—
Dread! labor! and the evening and the
wife —
That, by the war he did not make, are sold ;
He thinks not of a child’s small fingers, lest
He see the vision of a nursing breast.
Christ thought He saved the world by sacri-
fice
Of blood; and smaller Christs saved it
again.
When for His vesture legions threw the dice.
And Calvary east shadows on the plain.
Men wished them true —the kindly, happy lies
That now the tortured earth was free of
pain :
But many Christs the world, since Noah's
flood,
Has known to come in war and cleanse in
blood.
Flesh is but flesh, of man-God or of man.'
The nameless Christs that die to cleanse
the world
Know not the order, method, nor the plan
That to the eager trench of death has
hurled
Brother and brother since the world began.
Or since the first barbarian's flag un-
furled.
Our Herod and our l’ilate are but one—
The self-drunk king who owns the heaviest
gun.
A hundred years of order, self-control.
Fluxed in war’s crucible of molten hate ;
Christ! Moses! Biuldli! Genius from pole
to pole:
Plato! Beethoven ! Shakspeare! All the
great
Obscured by shadows that some puppet-soul
Makes till the melting-pot's grey fumes
abate:
Given to the grave the sculptors, painters,
too:
While man-made gods laugh down the cen-
tral blue.
* * * *
Hear girl, who hast tln* senses of the spring.
Who gra vest that October winds shall blow
Peach and pear blossom down to earth,
and fling
The fading flowers of the acacia low:
War hath its use, like any cleansing thing.
_ And all the meaner things of life shall go:
The fatted ease of all the hypocrites;
The smug content of all the huckstering cits.
Only shall live the great Bealities !
All royal charlatans shall disappear,
And literature arise, to truly seize
A world regenerated front the sere.
All the dead creeds in lumber-rooms at ease.
To wait their time when war again is here :
And some new king, to burn a new Louvain.
Invents a God of Battles once again!
Sweet, hate thou war because all youth is
clean.
And men are evil; greed has leached their
blood ;
Out of this lull the world shall rise serene.
Cant of all kings drowned in the battle
flood;
Prince pimp, and clay-brained king, and
dullard queen
Crackle to ashes in the furnace red;
And Demos rise, splendid in his new youth !
A child who’s lost the lie and found the
truth !
VICTORIA.
RANDOLPH BEDFORD.
